  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_aa8f6f4d-78cd-480a-9409-015a25107016'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText3439293835945556918" style="display:none">Quince años mas tarde, la memoria de aquel dia ha vuelto a mi. He visto a aquel muchacho vagando entre las brumas de la estacion de Francia y el nombre de Marina se ha encendido de nuevo como una herida fresca. Todos tenemos un secreto encerrado bajo llave en el atico del alma. este es el mio.<br /><br />En la Barcelona de 1980 Oscar Drai suena despierto, deslumbrado por los placeres mocernistas cercanos al internado en el que estudia. En una de sus escapadas conoce a Marina, una chica audaz que comparte con oscar la aventura de adentrarse en un enigma doloroso del pasado de la ciudad. Un misterioso personaje de la posguerra se propuso el mayor desafio imaginable, pero su ambicion lo arrastro por sendas siniestras cucyas consecuencias debe pagar alguien todavia hoy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3439293835945556918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_2255008013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2255008013" />
    <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance"><img alt="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513125058p2/68538597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2255008013?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780297856474" href="/book/show/17873946-marina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller">crime-mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2255008013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6926901605269768702"><b>Some authors just have IT.</b> <br/><br/><i>“The territory of humans is life. Death does not belong to us.”</i><br/><br/>This fine piece of well-crafted, chilling literature is set in Barcelona on the cusp of the 1980s, -although the magical, timeless quality also makes the story feel like it could be taking place at any time period -, and features many of the trappings of a gothic tale: doomed love, monstrous creatures, scientific experiments gone awry and, of course, trips through the sewers. <br/><br/>The book is written from Oscar </span>
  <span id="freeText6926901605269768702" style="display:none"><b>Some authors just have IT.</b> <br /><br /><i>“The territory of humans is life. Death does not belong to us.”</i><br /><br />This fine piece of well-crafted, chilling literature is set in Barcelona on the cusp of the 1980s, -although the magical, timeless quality also makes the story feel like it could be taking place at any time period -, and features many of the trappings of a gothic tale: doomed love, monstrous creatures, scientific experiments gone awry and, of course, trips through the sewers. <br /><br />The book is written from Oscar Drai's point of view, a fifteen-year-old boarding school pupil in Barcelona. Oscar wanders into the garden of what he assumes to be an abandoned house and meets Marina, a girl of his age, and her artist father Germán. <br />Oscar quickly forms a friendship with this eccentric family (as well as having a burgeoning crush on Marina), but the real intrigue begins when the mysterious and enigmatic Marina pulls him into a fascinating adventure as she leads him to a cemetery, where they watch a macabre ritual that occurs on the last Sunday of each month. At exactly ten o'clock in the morning, a veiled woman places a single rose on an unmarked grave. <br /><br />Pursuing the mystery of this act leads the two into an unimaginably twisted and grim adventure in Barcelona's underworld and a dark secret that lies beneath the city streets.<br />Zafón weaves reality and magic, science fiction, and superstition together smoothly and beautifully, where sorrow goes hand in hand with joy and excitement, telling a compelling story shaped in part by Barcelona itself-as with most of his other novels-, bringing the city to life for the reader while telling a tale that is ominous, melancholic, and at times terrible.<br /><br /><i>“We had reached the enchanted Barcelona, the labyrinth of spirits, where streets had mythical names and the ghosts of time walked behind us.”</i><br /><br />Zafón's narrative style is utterly captivating and the language that he employs is completely relatable. There’s a constant gothic undercurrent of madness, darkness and twisted imagination, while his atmospheric and incredibly evocative portrayal of Barcelona makes you feel as if you yourself are there experiencing everything along with the characters. <br /><br />He builds up a fascinating and elaborate world and then slowly, painstakingly tearing it down again in a way that you’ll most likely find sincerely heartbreaking. <br />Though the protagonist is a teenage boy and in some ways feels like a YA fantasy-esque story, it reads as a lot more grown-up, one written with the deliberate intent to appeal to a wider audience. <br /><br /><br /><br /><b>A few memorable quotes:</b><br /><br />⤗ <i>“Man’s meanness is a fuse in search of a flame.”</i><br /><br />⤗ <i>“We are doomed to remember what never really happened.”</i><br /><br />⤗ <i>“The public will always choose a warmed-up lie over the cold truth.”</i><br /><br />⤗ <i>“Time does to the body what stupidity does to the soul.”</i><br /><br />⤗ <i>“Our body begins to destroy itself from the moment it is born. We are fragile. We’re creatures of passage. All that is left of us are our actions, the good or the evil we do to our fellow humans.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6926901605269768702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17566244932066046969">Shorter but definitely darker than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1232.The_Shadow_of_the_Wind__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books__1_' title='The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Shadow of the Wind</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4912857.The_Angel_s_Game__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___2_' title='The Angel's Game (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #2) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Angel's Game</a>. I wish someone made an animation based on the book, it has tons of potential. I totally love the song <s>and have no idea who sings it. I might just google a bit.</s> Apparently it's Sia's My Love.<br/><br/></span>
  <span id="freeText17566244932066046969" style="display:none">Shorter but definitely darker than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1232.The_Shadow_of_the_Wind__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books__1_" title="The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow of the Wind</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4912857.The_Angel_s_Game__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___2_" title="The Angel's Game (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #2) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">The Angel's Game</a>.   <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1039546311" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1039546311" />
    <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan"><img alt="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553101944p2/4728718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1039546311?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan">Algernon (Darth Anyan)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780297856474" href="/book/show/17873946-marina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1039546311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13017548697543715463"><br/><i> In the late 1970s Barcelona was a mirage of avenues and winding alleys where one could easily travel thirty or forty years into the past by just stepping into the foyer of a grand old building or walking into a cafe. Time and memory, history and fiction merged in the enchanted city like watercolours in the rain. It was there, in the lingering echo of the streets that no longer exist, that cathedrals and age-old palaces created the tapestry into which this story would be woven. </i><br/><br/>Once more, Carlos</span>
  <span id="freeText13017548697543715463" style="display:none"><br /><i> In the late 1970s Barcelona was a mirage of avenues and winding alleys where one could easily travel thirty or forty years into the past by just stepping into the foyer of a grand old building or walking into a cafe. Time and memory, history and fiction merged in the enchanted city like watercolours in the rain. It was there, in the lingering echo of the streets that no longer exist, that cathedrals and age-old palaces created the tapestry into which this story would be woven. </i><br /><br />Once more, Carlos Ruiz Zafon chooses as his setting his beloved city of Barcelona, letting his imagination weave secret, fantastic and scary histories behind the facades of the old buildings. The flowing, organic, twisted plot line mirrors maybe the style of the city's other poet, the one who wrote his verses in stone - Antonio Gaudi. Marina precedes the Library of Forgotten books series and marks the transition from his Young Adult early novels to his more ambitious Shadow of the Wind. There is a lot of similarity between the protagonists, Oscar Drai here and Daniel Sempere in the later novel. Both have a vivid imagination and both love to roam the city streets at all hours. Both fall for mysterious girls, both get entangled in old conflicts with a touch of the supernatural, both stories start in a cemetery of sorts.<br /><br /><i>The memories of hundreds of people lie here. Their lives, their feelings, their expectations, their absence, the dreams that never came true for them, the disappointments, the deceptions and the unrequited loves that poisoned their existence ... All that is here, trapped forever. Nothing in life can be understood until you understand death. </i><br /><br />How's that for a first date? Boy meets beautiful girl, he invites her out and she takes him for a first date to an old, forgotten graveyard where they witness a masked lady, dressed all in black, lay a red rose on a grave marked only by the image of a black butterfly. There must be a story behind this mystery.<br /><br />I'd say she's a keeper! Grey-eyed Marina lives with her father, German Blau, in a huge house set in an untended garden. Her mother died giving birth to Marina, and the rooms are filled with her beautiful portraits, the last paintings ever to be done by her bereaved husband. Oscar takes about a couple of seconds to fall utterly and irreversibly in love with her, but she keeps him at a distance. The investigation into the secret of the veiled woman, the grave, the rose and the black butterfly will help to bring boy and girl closer together.<br /><br />The writing style took some getting used to, especially due to the heavy handed use of lurid adjectives and to the extraordinary circumstances the young couple has to face. After the forgotten graveyard, they investigate a 'macabre' greenhouse, a derelict apartment, an abandoned Opera House, a burned down luxury residence, the sewers under the city streets, a railway station (<i> I'd always thought that old railway stations were one of the few magical places left in the world, where ghosts of memories and farewells mingled with the start of hundreds of one-way journeys to faraway destinations. </i>). They almost get killed by a train inside a tunnel, by strange marionnetes half-human and half-machine, are hunted by evil smelling ghosts and reclusive taxi drivers.<br /><br /><i> The inside of the factory looked to me like the scene of a nightmare. Hundreds of feet, hands, arms, legs and glass eyes were scattered about the premises ... replacement parts for a broken and miserable humanity. </i><br /><br />These are just a few examples of the scary, yet so entertaining, adventures Oscar and Marina have as they unravel the history of Mijail Kolvenik and Eva Irinova. I will not give more details of this subject, better to have some surprises left out of my review. I will only say that the novel reminded me strongly of the XIX century Romantic movement, with its preference for tragic star-crossed lovers and grand gestures made by passionate souls ready to fight against Death in order to remain by the side of their lovers. I'm thinking of Victor Hugo (Notre Dame de Paris), of Gaston Leroux (The Phantom of the Opera), of Bram Stoker or Eugene Sue - powerful melodrama with lots of corpses and morbid settings. From my recent reads the closer comparison I can make is with Ysabel by Guy Gavriel Kay, another Y.A. adventure about a couple of youths investigating the ghosts of the past.<br /><br /><i> That night Mijail said he believed each one of us is only granted brief moments of pure happiness. Sometimes only days or weeks. Other times years. It all depends on our luck. The remembrance of such moments stays with us for ever and becomes a land of memories to which we vainly attempt to return during the rest of our existence. </i><br /><br />Parallel to the drama of Mijail and Irina, the boy and the girl are making their own history together, a more delicate and touching affair, with touches of humour in the beginning (<i> When her lips touched my ear I felt a tingling on the nape of my neck, like a centipede dancing the bossa nova. </i>) and a lot of sadness and pain later on (<i> Sometimes the things that are most real only happen in one's imagination, Oscar. We only remember what never really happened. </i>). History repeats itself, from Mijail and Irina, to the girls's parents German and Kirsten, to Oscar and Marina. The lovers are not destined for happy ever after. The moral of the story is to not be afraid of life, embrace it and cherish the moments together because they will be over much too soon. As an older German Blau remarks:<br /><br /><i> It's the fire of youth. Believe me, I envy you. Youth is like a fickle girlfriend. We can't understand or value her until she goes off with someone else, never to return ... </i><br /><br />Me too, at the end of the journey, feel it is better to remember Marina and Daniel for the vivacity and courage and curiosity about their surroundings that defined them rather than for <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the bittersweet pain of separation  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Conclusion : Marina can be a good choice as an introduction to Carlos Ruiz Zafon, an easier read but similar in style and content with the Shadow of the Wind, which remains my favorite.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13017548697543715463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_603554264" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/603554264" />
    <a title="Blair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/272909-blair"><img alt="Blair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493499323p2/272909.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/603554264?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blair" href="/user/show/272909-blair">Blair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18658819-marina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=2013-release">2013-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=macabre-slipstream-weird">macabre-slipstream-weird</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=translated">translated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer603554264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17627255892595955832"><a href='http://learnthisphrase.blogspot.com/2013/10/book-review-marina-by-carlos-ruiz-zafon.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review originally published at Learn This Phrase.</a><br/><br/><i>Marina</i> is the last of Carlos Ruiz Zafón's existing books to be translated into English, following the first three books of the Barcelona quartet (for adult readers), and the Niebla trilogy (for teenagers). Published in Spanish in 1999 - two years before the worldwide bestseller <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1232.The_Shadow_of_the_Wind__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___1_' title='The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Shadow of the Wind</a> - it is the final young adult novel written by the author, and its transitional nature is evident in the style. It reads as a lot more 'grown-up' tha</span>
  <span id="freeText17627255892595955832" style="display:none"><a href="http://learnthisphrase.blogspot.com/2013/10/book-review-marina-by-carlos-ruiz-zafon.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review originally published at Learn This Phrase.</a><br /><br /><i>Marina</i> is the last of Carlos Ruiz Zafón's existing books to be translated into English, following the first three books of the Barcelona quartet (for adult readers), and the Niebla trilogy (for teenagers). Published in Spanish in 1999 - two years before the worldwide bestseller <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1232.The_Shadow_of_the_Wind__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___1_" title="The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow of the Wind</a> - it is the final young adult novel written by the author, and its transitional nature is evident in the style. It reads as a lot more 'grown-up' than the Niebla books, but the protagonist is a teenage boy and in many ways this feels like a young adult fantasy story, albeit one written with the deliberate intent to appeal to a wider audience.<br /><br />Set primarily in between 1979 and 1980 - although it feels as though it could be a lot earlier - <i>Marina</i> is written from the point of view of Oscar Drai, a fifteen-year-old boarding school pupil in Barcelona. Lonely and bored, Oscar wanders into the garden of what he assumes to be an abandoned house and meets the beautiful, ethereal Marina, a girl of his age who is home-schooled, and her artist father Germán. Oscar is quickly drawn into a friendship with this eccentric, fascinating family (as well as having a burgeoning crush on Marina), but the real intrigue begins when Marina takes him to a nearby graveyard, where the pair watch a veiled woman place a single rose on an unmarked grave. Pursuing the mystery of this act leads the two friends into an unimaginably complex and macabre adventure in Barcelona's underworld.<br /><br />This is a classic Ruiz Zafón book in that it has so much going for it, so much to be fascinated by, yet never quite makes good on that promise, and - however much you might <i>want</i> it to be - just isn't as good as it <i>should</i> be with all the brilliant ingredients that have been thrown into it. More than any of his others, this particular book seems to highlight very clearly what is both good and bad about the author's writing.<br /><br /><b>The good:</b><br />- Such rich, descriptive prose: often verging on over-the-top, flowery language, but incredibly enjoyable to lose yourself in, and lacking the awkwardness of much translated fiction.<br />- A constant gothic undercurrent of madness, darkness and twisted imagination.<br />- Atmospheric and incredibly evocative portrayal of Barcelona.<br />- A magical, timeless quality which makes the story feel like it could be taking place in any time period.<br /><br /><b>The bad:</b><br />- Poorly drawn, underdeveloped female characters who are all unrealistically flawless, fragile and virginal.<br />- Confused action scenes that become incomprehensible in places.<br />- The overall plot becomes so complicated and bogged down in different subplots and characters' stories that it's easy to lose track of what is actually supposed to be happening.<br /><br />I did enjoy <i>Marina</i> - but, as usual, not as much as I wished I could. With its rich, ominous mixture of characters, places, dreadful misdeeds and weird stuff, it makes for a largely compelling read that doesn't feel compelling as a whole - I felt deflated when I reached the end, and cared little about any of the characters. It feels a bit churlish to complain about characters being two-dimensional in a novel that would be more suited to a reader half my age, but so much attention seems to have been paid to the descriptive details of the settings that the people it's all supposed to revolve around have been neglected. It's telling that the book is named for Marina yet, having read it, I have nothing whatsoever to say about that character. I wasn't sure about the fantasy element, either (again, this would probably be far more enjoyable and frightening to the hypothetical younger reader), and one thing that happened near the end was so ridiculously clichéd and terrible that I nearly lost my patience completely.<br /><br />I was drawn to <i>Marina</i> by the same things that have made me read almost all of Ruiz Zafón's books, and I was disappointed by the exact same things that have disappointed me in the author's other work - a feeling that the whole thing is more about style than substance, and terrible female characters. It's bound to be a hit with die-hard fans of the author since it offers so many similarities with the rest of his books: admittedly, it's interesting to see many of the themes of his adult fiction emerging here, and it would probably make a good starting point for those unfamiliar with <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i> et al. I'm not wholly convinced that <i>Marina</i> lives up to the tagline on the cover which declares it to be 'a gothic tale for all ages', but it's a fun read, if a frustratingly imperfect one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17627255892595955832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText18098250320977464836" style="display:none">I just find this a brilliant book, and its not only because it has the most awesome name like, ever (my name lol) but I think it has a beautiful mixture of many genres, like it has a small dose of romance, sci-fi, mystery, thriller, drama that in a whole make it a book completely delicious and easy to read.<br /><br />The fact that it can mix sci-fi, with the teenage romance and give it all a total mystery hunter style is priceless.           <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22176981-olivera?shelf=2017">2017</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1310654705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5731625259096040946">This is the second book by Zafon that I've read (the first one being The Prince of Mist), and this time around it hit my taste a bit better. There is this magic happening in the way the author writes Barcelona, which I loved very much. Now I'm just longing for more books with European settings. <br/><br/>Anyways, the ending is what made this book for me. While the twist wasn't so unexpected, it did still hit me very hard and I have a feeling that it will stick with me for a while. <br/><br/>Marina is a gothic story</span>
  <span id="freeText5731625259096040946" style="display:none">This is the second book by Zafon that I've read (the first one being The Prince of Mist), and this time around it hit my taste a bit better. There is this magic happening in the way the author writes Barcelona, which I loved very much. Now I'm just longing for more books with European settings. <br /><br />Anyways, the ending is what made this book for me. While the twist wasn't so unexpected, it did still hit me very hard and I have a feeling that it will stick with me for a while. <br /><br />Marina is a gothic story, beautifully told with very likable characters that all have intriguing pasts. There were parts of the book that scared me quite a lot (hey, I'm a huge chicken when it comes to this), but I was so attached to the individual stories of the characters that I just didn't mind. In my opinion, the whole book would have been better if Zafon had just stuck with a contemporary tale, rather than a supernatural one. <br /><br />While this author hasn't blown me away, like he has so many of my friends here on Goodreads, I would still like to check out some more of his books, with The Shadow of the Wind being my next read of his. <br /><br /><i> I'm counting this for the Around the World in 80 Books challenge as a book set in Spain. </i></span>

<div id="review_1403969349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1403969349" />
    <a title="Asghar Abbas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37421322-asghar-abbas"><img alt="Asghar Abbas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444319622p2/37421322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1403969349?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Asghar Abbas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Asghar Abbas" href="/user/show/37421322-asghar-abbas">Asghar Abbas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316044714" href="/book/show/18349883-marina">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1403969349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1559833061952073498"><br/>Okay, where do I stand on this ? Wait, lemme get my breath back. Wow. What youthful emotions permeated in this book, raw. This was an excellent novel, clearly a beloved of the author's. It wasn't epic on Shadow of the Wind's scale, but still without much comparing them, it's a fine early work with enough unique wordlings in it to pack quite a few punches, whew. <br/><br/>I don't think this was a Gothic tale per se, but still couple of times during the night it definitely crept me out, had to finish it dur</span>
  <span id="freeText1559833061952073498" style="display:none"><br />Okay, where do I stand on this ? Wait, lemme get my breath back. Wow. What youthful emotions permeated in this book, raw. This was an excellent novel, clearly a beloved of the author's. It wasn't epic on Shadow of the Wind's scale, but still without much comparing them, it's a fine early work with enough unique wordlings in it to pack quite a few punches, whew. <br /><br />I don't think this was a Gothic tale per se, but still couple of times during the night it definitely crept me out, had to finish it during the day, hehe. I feel the two connecting backstories were well told and on par with the central story. This book. Ahem. Um. Made me feel lonely, scared, isolated, sad and then made me fall in love with words again. <br /><br />Ultimately it ended up making me feel hopeful toward all things, especially friendships and good people made special, again and again. If we have the willingness to try, that is. <br /><br />Carlos Ruiz Zafon amazes me with his talents. I hate to admit that, so there it is. He is fantastic. One thing I have noticed; he loves women without betraying his gender or theirs. Bravo. <br /><br />It's kinda book that makes one wants to be a writer. Sadly, I am one already. And that is saddening indeed, but for all the reasons that's got naught to do with Words. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1559833061952073498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1020808766" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1020808766" />
    <a title="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede"><img alt="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487436758p2/1379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1020808766?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" href="/user/show/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede">Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789174294" href="/book/show/22754297-marina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1020808766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3469233327889133403"><i>15-year-old Óscar disappears in May 1980 from his boarding school in Barcelona. During seven days and seven nights, no one knows where he is...</i><br/> <br/>Marina is the fourth book I have read by Carlos Ruiz Zafón (not counting The Rose of Fire since it’s a short story) and I think it’s probably the best I have read of him. This book has nothing to do with The Cemetery of Forgotten Books series. But I don’t mind that, it's refreshing to read something different. The story takes place in Barcelona just like</span>
  <span id="freeText3469233327889133403" style="display:none"><i>15-year-old Óscar disappears in May 1980 from his boarding school in Barcelona. During seven days and seven nights, no one knows where he is...</i><br /> <br />Marina is the fourth book I have read by Carlos Ruiz Zafón (not counting The Rose of Fire since it’s a short story) and I think it’s probably the best I have read of him. This book has nothing to do with The Cemetery of Forgotten Books series. But I don’t mind that, it's refreshing to read something different. The story takes place in Barcelona just like The Cemetery of Forgotten Books does but this is years later and the story has nothing to do with forgotten books instead this is a love story. Or love stories, one in the present 1980’s Barcelona and one in the past, both tragic.<br /><br />This is one hell of a well-written book with a story that really spoke to me; tragic love stories, revenge, scary dolls, experiments, murder and a mystery woman in black with a tragic past. I just wish I could find more books like this.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3469233327889133403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1003863493" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1003863493" />
    <a title="TL " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4342402-tl"><img alt="TL " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587334107p2/4342402.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1003863493?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TL " class="user" itemprop="url" name="TL " href="/user/show/4342402-tl">TL </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316044714" href="/book/show/18349883-marina">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4342402-tl?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1003863493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2078333264067901713">4.5 actually, :) My favorite of these sets of books.. tied with 'watcher in the shadows'..Oscar and Marina are two of my favorite MCs of his.<br/><br/>*minor spoilers abound*<br/>---<br/><br/>A bit darker than the previous installments with some genuinely disturbing/horrifying moments, 'Marina' is an enchanting tale. Wonderfully tragic, suspenseful... bound with some romance as well.<br/><br/>Its always bittersweet for me in a way to finish a Carlos Ruiz Zafon tale... I love going on the journey and seeing what happens to everyon</span>
  <span id="freeText2078333264067901713" style="display:none">4.5 actually, :) My favorite of these sets of books.. tied with 'watcher in the shadows'..Oscar and Marina are two of my favorite MCs of his.<br /><br />*minor spoilers abound*<br />---<br /><br />A bit darker than the previous installments with some genuinely disturbing/horrifying moments, 'Marina' is an enchanting tale. Wonderfully tragic, suspenseful... bound with some romance as well.<br /><br />Its always bittersweet for me in a way to finish a Carlos Ruiz Zafon tale... I love going on the journey and seeing what happens to everyone, but at the same time I'm sad to leave them even though I know I can/will revisit them.<br /><br />Mister Zafon says it well here:<br /><b>"But soon after embarking on Marina I knew that this would be the last I'd write in the genre. As the writing advanced, everything in the story began to acquire a shade of farewell, and by the time I'd finished it, I sensed that something inside me---something that even today I cannot explain but that I still miss every single day-- was forever left among its pages." </b><br /><br />You can feel his writing mature and grow among these series of books, 'the prince of mist', 'the midnight palace', and <br />the watcher in the shadows'... growing into his craft and branching out bit by bit... 'Marina' feels closer of sorts to the style he will use in 'Shadow of the Wind'<br /><br />I do admit wishing that sometimes the people in his story would have a happy ending haha but that's also what is so beautiful about this narrative and his others, the sense of tragedy/foreboding/humanity.<br />````````<br /><i>"Marina once told me that we only remember what never really happened. It would take me a lifetime to understand what those words meant. But I suppose I'd better start at the beginning, in which this case is the end.<br /><br />In May 1980 I disappeared from the world for an entire week. For seven days and seven nights nobody knew my whereabouts."<br /><br />"We all have a secret buried lock and key in the attic of our soul, this is mine." </i><br /><br />This starts the us on the journey of Oscar Drai in Barcelona... his first meeting with German Blau is unexpected and he 'accidentally' ends up stealing the man's pocket watch. It is when he goes to return that he meets German's daughter 'Marina' and properly meets the man himself.<br /><br />The mystery takes off when Marina takes Oscar to an old cemetery and they observe a lady shrouded in black lay a rose on an unmarked gravestone.<br /><br />What they don't expect is to be transported into a baffling mystery that plunges them in a strange/terrifying world and its too late to turn back when the mystery starts pursuing them.<br /><br />The story unfolds at a steady place, letting you get to know the people involved and dropping hints and information here and there, leaving you eager to know what happens to everyone. I had a shaky reading time with this, only because I kept getting interrupted ;-) haha but when I did have time, it was very hard to put this down.<br /><br />You feel for everyone involved, even Kolvenik... despicable man for what he was doing and it was horrifying when he revealed his work at a certain part of the story. As what happened to him was revealed though, you understand and sympathize with him... and it does seem as if he was meant for this/cursed. He started out trying to do good but ended up being consumed by his genetics I guess you could say.<br /><br />Mister Zafon had me guessing and changing my perceptions constantly in this story. Whenever I had a suspicion of what was going on, he turned it on its head and the story went in another direction. A couple of things caught me by surprise completely.<br /><br />A few of the characters I thought deserved their fates... no sympathy for them even though you can see/understood their motives.<br /><br />I loved following in Oscar and Marina's footsteps, untangling the whole affair with them. Marina was sometimes cold and distant towards Oscar but on the whole I loved her (the reason for her behavior is explained later). Oscar was an interesting young man, lonely and adrift.. Marina and German become his 'family' of sorts.<br /><br />Layers upon layers is one way of describing this book. Each time something is uncovered, something else is there to surprise you and lead you merrily (or not so merrily down another path).<br /><br />The ending was a race through the pages for me and I thought a fitting end for that part of the story. I felt a relief and sadness at the same time.<br /><br />Marina and Oscar had me smiling/sighing/wistful at the same time. The last paragraph is good ending for Oscar's part of the story, brings it full circle I guess you could say.<br /><br />I'm rambling haha but I hope I conveyed my love of this book well enough. Highly recommend! :) &lt;3<br /><br />I'll leave youins with a few quotes from Marina: <br />____<br /><i>"Our body begins to destroy itself from the moment it is born. We are fragile. We're creatures of passage. All that is left of us are our actions, the good and evil we do to our fellow humans. "<br /><br />"We had reached the enchanted Barcelona, the labyrinth of spirits, where streets had mythical names and the ghosts of time walked behind us."</i><br /><br />*excuse any typos please*</span>
  <a data-text-id="2078333264067901713" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1215968200" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1215968200" />
    <a title="Pamela  (Here to Read Books and Chew Gum)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5927588-pamela-here-to-read-books-and-chew-gum"><img alt="Pamela  (Here to Read Books and Chew Gum)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600689816p2/5927588.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1215968200?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela  (Here to Read Books and Chew Gum)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela  (Here to Read Books and Chew Gum)" href="/user/show/5927588-pamela-here-to-read-books-and-chew-gum">Pamela  (Here to Read Books and Chew Gum)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781780224268" href="/book/show/22353192-marina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5927588-pamela-here-to-read-books-and-chew-gum?shelf=cross-over-fiction">cross-over-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5927588-pamela-here-to-read-books-and-chew-gum?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5927588-pamela-here-to-read-books-and-chew-gum?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5927588-pamela-here-to-read-books-and-chew-gum?shelf=macabre">macabre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5927588-pamela-here-to-read-books-and-chew-gum?shelf=modern-fairy-tales">modern-fairy-tales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1215968200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3825370742795246597">For a book that has been described as the best Zafon since 'The Shadow of the Wind' there are simply no words to describe what a consummate disappointment the experience of reading 'Marina' was. It was a book with so much potential that simply went nowhere, with two dimensional characters while being completely derivative of much greater works. It was completely unoriginal and such a disappointment to read.<br/><br/>I am always wary with translated books, as they do seem to lose a lot in the method of tra</span>
  <span id="freeText3825370742795246597" style="display:none">For a book that has been described as the best Zafon since 'The Shadow of the Wind' there are simply no words to describe what a consummate disappointment the experience of reading 'Marina' was. It was a book with so much potential that simply went nowhere, with two dimensional characters while being completely derivative of much greater works. It was completely unoriginal and such a disappointment to read.<br /><br />I am always wary with translated books, as they do seem to lose a lot in the method of translation. I feel that perhaps this may be the case with Zafon's 'Marina' as most Spanish reviews seem to give it glowing praise. Perhaps there is something about the language and descriptions in the Spanish language that give this novel a depth which it lacks in English. Or perhaps that Zafon's labour of love was translated by someone else, rather than the author himself made it lose a little of its impact.<br /><br />The pacing of 'Marina' is way off. It starts with Oscar being mysteriously discovered alone in a train station by a policeman, unwilling to talk about the recent ordeal which had him missing without a trace for a week. We would hope that this mystery would have a thrilling resolution, however the reason for the week's disappearance is truly mundane as we find out toward the end of the novel. The mystery which is unrelated to Oscar's disappearance is also never solved organically. Instead, we follow the protagonists Oscar and Marina from secondary character, to secondary character who give us all the relevant information we need to know in long, convenient soliloquies with no apparent reason for doing so. <br /><br />We are given no sense of character for anyone in the novel. We know nothing about Oscar or Marina other than they exist in this one moment. The novel seems to be narrated by an adult Oscar, but we don't even know what he went on to become, or how this tale effected his life to the point where he felt it had to be told. The motivations for secondary characters to give these two teenagers all the information they ask for are non-existent, indeed in some cases I would go so far as to say it would be a breach of confidentiality to have given these two teenagers any of the information. A policeman decided to give a random 15 year old information about an ongoing corporate investigation, and a doctor decides to share the patient details of not only a patient, but his friend? Any why? Because they asked nicely? The set ups for this information simply beggars belief. Zafon's female characters are appallingly written; he is very old fashioned in his descriptions of women who always remain white, virginal and fragile. The pedestal grates after a while.<br /><br />When I say this book is derivative, it is because it smacks of unoriginality. The two most glaring comparisons can come from Mary Shelley's 'Frankenstein' (to the point where there is a doctor Shelley who's daughter is conveniently named Maria...) with motif's of the creation of life, what playing god can mean for yourself and those around you, and the monstrosities created when you play god. The second most notable parallel is between 'Marina' and Gaston Leroux's 'The Phantom of the Opera'. We have the setting of an opulent theatre, the theme of physical deformity, even some vague allusions to 'carnival freaks' which is never really properly developed other than providing a convenient McGuffin of the discovery of an old photo album full of pictures of those with physical deformities, which Marina and Oscar, quite untastefully, continuously describe as 'horrific' (which also never goes anywhere in the plot...)<br /><br />This book had potential, but to say that potential was not reached is almost understating it. What an absolute disappointment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3825370742795246597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1343087826" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1343087826" />
    <a title="Gabrielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6753400-gabrielle"><img alt="Gabrielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598976963p2/6753400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1343087826?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabrielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabrielle" href="/user/show/6753400-gabrielle">Gabrielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780297856474" href="/book/show/17873946-marina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=own-a-copy">own-a-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=ouch-my-feels">ouch-my-feels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1343087826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15745016432790987041">Carlos, why do you do this to my feels?!<br/><br/>If I had read this book when I was the age of it's intented audience (13 to 17), I would probably have loved it even more. Now I can see that he uses some tropes that I am already familiar with because of my adoration for "Shadow of the Wind" and I am a bit disenchanted with his female characters, but you know what? I don't care! This book still crushed me and I still got lost in his labyrinthian descriptions of Barcelona, in his abandonned mansions and ta</span>
  <span id="freeText15745016432790987041" style="display:none">Carlos, why do you do this to my feels?!<br /><br />If I had read this book when I was the age of it's intented audience (13 to 17), I would probably have loved it even more. Now I can see that he uses some tropes that I am already familiar with because of my adoration for "Shadow of the Wind" and I am a bit disenchanted with his female characters, but you know what? I don't care! This book still crushed me and I still got lost in his labyrinthian descriptions of Barcelona, in his abandonned mansions and tales of cursed love. Some might say that this is penny dreadful material, and they wouldn't be wrong. There are graveyards, creepy abandoned factories and greenhouses, a mad scientist, some Russian thugs… Where "The Angel's Game" had the sweet smell of Bronte and Dickens all over it, "Marina" is liberally perfumed with Stoker, Hugo and Leroux's influence: romantic, lurid and melodramatic. In other words, it's awesome!<br /><br />Oscar meets Marina exploring what he believes to be an abandoned garden, only to find the attached mansion inhabitated by this lovely girl and her sickly, artsy father, German. Obviously, he falls in love with her, but she keeps him at a distance and a friendship develops. One evening, as they are visiting an old graveyard (because that's an amazing thing to do, duh!), they witness a scene that seems to have been lifted from the pages of a Gothic novel: a veiled woman in a black dress leaves a single red rose on a namelss grave, marked only with a black butterfly. Because young people are curious and don't know any better, Oscar and Marina decide to investigate this strange event… Because this is a Zafon novel (YA or not), they find a lot more than they bargained for, and what they find is terrifying, tragic and they might just pay for their curiousity with their lives.<br /><br />As with his other novels, the past and the present events mirror each other oddly: lovers are not meant for happy endings in Zafon's books, but the man writes with such grandiose and rich beauty that putting the book down is impossible. He captures something about the almost ridiculous intensity of first loves that gets me every time. His plot lines twist and blend into each other artfully, he adds a touch of supernatural to make you shudder… and then he rips your heart out.<br /><br />I know I am a complete fangirl, but if Gothic mysteries are your thing and you love beautiful, ornate language that creates an atmospheric read you can almost drown into, look no further and read some Carlos Ruiz Zafon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15745016432790987041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2174896012" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2174896012" />
    <a title="Al" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29826097-al"><img alt="Al" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482412006p2/29826097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2174896012?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Al" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Al" href="/user/show/29826097-al">Al</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2174896012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8623300447646619501">Devastating. All of life we run from death and the idea of it but when we are forced to face the grief of loss we realise we knew all along how it feels. At least I did. <br/>This book is melancholic and filled me with nostalgia for Barcelona, for lost love, for times past and oddly for opera. I believe this is the last YA book the author wrote and throughout there is a sense of journey into adulthood, of saying goodbye. Ah, life! The things we do to one another. <br/>Truly unique. I miss it already. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1603303343" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1603303343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11002059935519755769">Carlos Ruiz Zafon's "Marina" has something for everyone. It's part gothic horror, part mystery, part historical fiction, part love story. It will make you shudder and make you cry (or at least, it did me!) The atmosphere is brilliantly maintained throughout, and the descriptions are often breathtaking. <br/><br/>I listened to the audiobook, narrated by Daniel Weyman, and would recommend that format as I thought he did a great job.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer3819840762768451635">2 stars--meh.<br/><br/>I think this is a case of "it's not you, it's me." This book HAS all the things I usually like--horror elements, a truly creepy villain, and lots of gothic trappings.<br/><br/>However, it didn't really hold my attention. There was lots of running--characters constantly fleeing one horror or another--with little sense to it, as well as too many minor characters. Generally, I was just confused. Even though it's a short book, it felt long. <br/><br/>I think part of the problem was I listened on audio, and</span>
  <span id="freeText3819840762768451635" style="display:none">2 stars--meh.<br /><br />I think this is a case of "it's not you, it's me." This book HAS all the things I usually like--horror elements, a truly creepy villain, and lots of gothic trappings.<br /><br />However, it didn't really hold my attention. There was lots of running--characters constantly fleeing one horror or another--with little sense to it, as well as too many minor characters. Generally, I was just confused. Even though it's a short book, it felt long. <br /><br />I think part of the problem was I listened on audio, and though the reader was good, I went out of town and got busy and wouldn't listen for days on end, so it was hard to remember what was happening. Again, not the book's fault. <br /><br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_730130069" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/730130069" />
    <a title="Damian Dubois" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3481936-damian-dubois"><img alt="Damian Dubois" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594640113p2/3481936.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/730130069?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Damian Dubois" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Damian Dubois" href="/user/show/3481936-damian-dubois">Damian Dubois</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781922079152" href="/book/show/18589054-marina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3481936-damian-dubois?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer730130069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16694456755171267557">I must say that I received a pleasant surprise just last week when scanning the shelves at my local book store my eyes alighted on a rather striking cover of a book titled <i>Marina</i> (I have always loved that name), a new novella by the wonderful Carlos Ruiz Zafón. Only, it's not new at all. First published in 1999, it has now only just been translated and published in English, no doubt on the back of his international best seller, <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i>. Needless to say I snatched up that book quic</span>
  <span id="freeText16694456755171267557" style="display:none">I must say that I received a pleasant surprise just last week when scanning the shelves at my local book store my eyes alighted on a rather striking cover of a book titled <i>Marina</i> (I have always loved that name), a new novella by the wonderful Carlos Ruiz Zafón. Only, it's not new at all. First published in 1999, it has now only just been translated and published in English, no doubt on the back of his international best seller, <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i>. Needless to say I snatched up that book quick smart and devoured it in a day or two.<br /><br />The story is told in the first person from the perspective of Oscar Drai, a fifteen-year old boy languishing in a boarding school named after some half forgotten saint on the hills of Vallvidrera. Having just written that line out an old Pet Shop Boys song just sprung into my head - This Must Be the Place I Waited Years to Leave. Obviously the title goes hand in hand with Oscar's listlessness at school but the line, "I'm listening to the words I thought I'd never hear again / A litany of saints and other ordinary men" just seems to go with the naming of the school. Love that song. But I digress...<br /><br />Bored with his lot in life and constantly watching out for the clock to hit that magical twenty past five each day, Oscar decides to explore the city with every chance he gets. On one particular escapade Oscar finds himself venturing down one of these lanes, past dilapidated art nouvea mansions that have seen the rise and fall of family dynasties, finding himself before a rusted iron gate, behind which resides a weed choked garden from years of neglect. His curiosity gets the better of him when he hears the soft tones of an aria accompanied by a lady’s beautiful voice. Drawn in by this hypnotic sound, he follows the voice into a candle-lit conservatory where he discovers a record playing on a gramophone next to which is an old antique time piece. His reverie is shattered when he finds that he is not the only one in the room and in a panic he flees back to the boarding school only to find out later that he has taken the time piece with him.<br /><br />Feeling guilty about having ‘stolen’ the watch he sets out to return the item and it's whilst on this endeavour that he meets a young girl (slightly older, 17) by the name of Marina who quickly identifies Oscar as the ‘watch thief’, the owner being her father, Germán Blau.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I turned round and beheld a vision straight out of a dream. A bicycle was slowly emerging out of the mist. A young girl clad in a vaporous white dress was pedalling up the hill towards me. In the early sunlight I could almost make out her silhouette through the cotton. Her long straw-coloured hair waved about, concealing her face. I stood there, immobile, watching her as she approached, rooted to the ground like a fool. The bicycle stopped a few metres away. My eyes, or my imagination, spied the shape of slim legs as she stepped down. Slowly, I took in every part of that dress – which looked like something out of a Sorolla painting – until my eyes rested on the girl’s deep grey eyes, so deep you could fall into them. They were riveted on mine with a sarcastic look. I gawped at her, smilingly stupidly.<br /><br />“You must be the watch thief.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Apologies and introductions aside, Marina invites Oscar to share in on a mystery she has discovered and is keen to share with someone. For at precisely 10 a.m. on the fourth Sunday of each month, a coach pulled by black horses appears. A woman dressed in black, her face concealed by a veil, deposits a single red rose on a tombstone bearing no name but is mysteriously emblazoned with the symbol of a single black butterfly. And thus the journey begins...<br /><br />Much like <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i> the story unfolds with the introduction of new characters and by recounting their prospective involvement in the central mystery at large, we find the level of intrigue and suspense only intensifies. Our three main characters (Oscar, Marina and Germán) are very well written and you can’t help but be drawn into their lives and worrying and caring about them. The character of Oscar really reminded me of Daniel Sempere from Shadow and while some people might label this a fault of the author not being able to write different characters, I found the similarity, and therefore the familiarity, rather comforting. I guess having enjoyed Daniel’s story also helped in that regards as well. The interaction between Oscar and Marina was handled very well and their feelings for another felt natural and in no way forced. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And because of Oscar’s growing feelings for Marina the ending of the novel became a very touching and poignant moment for me and I’m unashamed to admit shedding a tear or two.<br /><blockquote><i>At daybreak, with the first light of dawn, Marina pressed my hand hard, smiled at her father, and the flame in her eyes went out for ever</i></blockquote> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Before I sum this up I just want to make mention of a certain scene that I found absolutely chilling, something that really added to the whole Gothic flavour of the tale. I’ll wrap this also in spoilers just in case you want to experience the thrill for the first time as well...<br /><blockquote>
  <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
    <i>We exchanged glances and slowly raised our eyes to look at a shadowy area in the roof of the glasshouse. We were surrounded by angular figures dangling in the void. I could see a dozen of them, perhaps more. Legs, arms, hands and eyes shining in the dark. A whole pack of lifeless bodies swung over us. When they brushed against one another they produced that soft metallic sound. We took a step back, and before we knew what was happening Marina had caught her ankle on a lever connected to a pulley system. The lever gave way. In a tenth of a second an army of frozen figures dropped into the space below. I threw myself over Marina to protect her and we both fell flat on our faces. The whole place shuddered violently and I could hear the roar of the old glass structure as it vibrated. I was afraid that the glass panes would shatter and a rain of shards would skewer us to the ground. Just then something cold touched the back of my neck. Fingers.<br /><br />I opened my eyes. A face was smiling at me. Bright yellow eyes flashed. They were lifeless. Glass eyes in a face carved out of lacquered wood. I heard Marina stifle a scream next to me.<br /><br />“They’re dolls,” I said, almost breathless.</i>
   <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</blockquote><br />So, overall another great story from the pen of Carlos Ruiz Zafón who is fast becoming one of my favourite authors. He simply has a fantastic way with words. Definitely recommended for anyone out there that loves a creepy, Gothic horror story loaded with mystery and a little romance thrown in for good measure. And this probably doesn't need to be said, but if you read <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i> and enjoyed it then <i>Marina</i> should also be right up your alley.<br /><br />4/5 stars.<br /><br />PS: The book is set in the 1980's but I swear I felt at times like I was back in an earlier century. This is by no means a criticism of the novel but more the fact that I didn't think there were many things that established it being set in that time period.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16694456755171267557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/748601849" />
    <a title="Dale Harcombe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800708-dale-harcombe"><img alt="Dale Harcombe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380932680p2/4800708.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/748601849?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dale Harcombe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dale Harcombe" href="/user/show/4800708-dale-harcombe">Dale Harcombe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780297856474" href="/book/show/17873946-marina">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer748601849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7640544782191805912"> The cover of this book is enough of a reason to want to read it. I adored the cover. As to the book itself, it is hard to describe. Much of the writing is extremely beautiful. It feels like reading poetry as the writing is so rich in imagery. The depiction of Marina’s lips touching Oscar’s ear is described as ‘tingling on the nape of my neck, like a centipede dancing the bossa nova.’ Or this quote from Quim Salvat, who in earlier times had been a mentor to Marina’s artist father, ‘Beauty is a b</span>
  <span id="freeText7640544782191805912" style="display:none"> The cover of this book is enough of a reason to want to read it. I adored the cover. As to the book itself, it is hard to describe. Much of the writing is extremely beautiful. It feels like reading poetry as the writing is so rich in imagery. The depiction of Marina’s lips touching Oscar’s ear is described as ‘tingling on the nape of my neck, like a centipede dancing the bossa nova.’ Or this quote from Quim Salvat, who in earlier times had been a mentor to Marina’s artist father, ‘Beauty is a breath of air that blows against the wind of reality.’ Some of the descriptions are so apt you can almost hear them like that of the sound in the greenhouse, ‘A metallic murmur, like the sound of a Venetian blind quivering.’ Those of us who have ever had Venetians know exactly what that sounds like.<br />I found myself agreeing with Marina’s father when he says’ ‘What sort of technology is this that can send a man to the moon but can’t put a piece of bread on every human being’s table?’ There are also light touches of humour as in when encountering a cat that stares at him with disdain, Oscar wishes he was a Doberman.<br />Along with the humour and the beautiful writing, there is also the macabre. But this is a gothic tale. Set in Barcelona in 1980 Oscar, a fifteen year school boy, finds himself drawn into the lives of the beautiful Marina, and her father. Oscar and Marina while trying to solve the mystery of the woman in black who places a single rose on a grave that bears no name, but only a black butterfly emblem, find themselves in a world of secrets. Some of the incidents and scenes are quite gruesome.<br />It also shows how power and knowledge that start with good intentions can become corrupted. <br />It is also a book filled with tales of love and sadness, as the love story of several sets of people are revealed. As I said, it is a book that is hard to classify. I loved it even though I found some of the more macabre scenes hard to read. With a vivid imagination, it’s not the sort of book I’d want to read before bedtime but it well worth reading. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7640544782191805912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
